"The &squot;New&squot; Face of Italy: Towards a Policy of Inclusion?"
Talk by Dr. Chiara Minestrelli, Visiting Scholar in Africana and Global Studies at Lehigh University.

Immigrants are changing the face of Italian culture, and yet the Italian media often portray stories of reticence, violence and segregation. The second generation of immigrants, born and raised in Italy, has been actively voicing their concerns with regard to their status as "second-class" citizens. Many have used music to address such concerns.

Dr. Minestrelli will address these topics, as well as that of the experiences of those Italians who choose to leave the country in search of a better future elsewhere.

Talk is free and open to the public. This event is sponsored by the Languages, Literatures &amp; Cultures Dept. and the Italian Studies Program.&squot;' width="532" height="333" />

                      <div id="id_583f5636db5125e85502037" class="text_exposed_root">
                       <p>
                        Friday, Dec. 2, 2-3pm in GQ Annex
                       </p>
                       <p>
                        &quot;The &#039;New&#039; Face of Italy: Towards a Policy of Inclusion?&quot;
                        <br />
                        Talk by Dr. Chiara Minestrelli, Visiting Scholar in Africana and Global Studies at Lehigh University.
                       </p>
                       <span class="text_exposed_hide">
                        ...
                       </span>
                       <div class="text_exposed_show">
                        <p>
                         Immigrants are changing the face of Italian culture, and yet the Italian media often portray stories of reticence, violence and segregation. The second generation of immigrants, born and raised in Italy, has been actively voicing their concerns with regard to their status as &quot;second-class&quot; citizens. Many have used music to address such concerns.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         Dr. Minestrelli will address these topics, as well as that of the experiences of those Italians who choose to leave the country in search of a better future elsewhere.
                        </p>
                        <p>
                         Talk is free and open to the public. This event is sponsored by the Languages, Literatures &amp; Cultures Dept. and the Italian Studies Program.
                        </p>
                       </div>

                                Powder Tossed at Metropolitan Opera May Have Been Human Ashes, Police Say
                               </a>

                               The Metropolitan Opera canceled a show before the final act after a man sprinkled a powdery substance into the orchestra pit.
